        <h2>Storyline</h2>
        
        <div class="inline canwrap" itemprop="description">
            <p>
When his brother is killed in a robbery, paraplegic Marine Jake Sully decides to take his place in a mission on the distant world of Pandora. There he learns of greedy corporate figurehead Parker Selfridge's intentions of driving off the native humanoid "Na'vi" in order to mine for the precious material scattered throughout their rich woodland. In exchange for the spinal surgery that will fix his legs, Jake gathers intel for the cooperating military unit spearheaded by gung-ho Colonel Quaritch, while simultaneously attempting to infiltrate the Na'vi people with the use of an "avatar" identity. While Jake begins to bond with the native tribe and quickly falls in love with the beautiful alien Neytiri, the restless Colonel moves forward with his ruthless extermination tactics, forcing the soldier to take a stand - and fight back in an epic battle for the fate of Pandora.                <em class="nobr">Written by
<a href="/search/title?plot_author=The+Massie+Twins&view=simple&sort=alpha&ref_=tt_stry_pl"
>The Massie Twins</a></em>            </p>
        </div>
        
        <span class="see-more inline"> 
                <a href="/title/tt0499549/plotsummary?ref_=tt_stry_pl"

        <h2>Did You Know?</h2>
    <div id="trivia" class="txt-block">
        <h4>Trivia</h4>


<a href="/name/nm0453746?ref_=tt_trv_trv">Yunjin Kim</a> appeared as Neytiri in early test footage.        <a href="trivia?ref_=tt_trv_trv"
class="nobr" >See more</a>  &raquo;
    </div>
                <hr />
     <div id="goofs"  class="txt-block">
        <h4>Goofs</h4>
In the scene right after the destruction of home-tree, when the people in the link room cancel the link in progress and Jake Sullys Avatar body goes limp, his Avatar is lying on his back with his head facing toward the left side of his body. Later, when the whole crew is able to escape the jail cell and move the mountain side base, Jake links back up with his Avatar and his head is facing straight up.        <a href="trivia?tab=gf&ref_=tt_trv_gf"
class="nobr" >See more</a>  &raquo;
    </div>   
                <hr />
    <div id="quotes" class="text-block">
        <h4>Quotes</h4>
[<span class="fine">first lines</span>]
<br /><a href="/name/nm0941777/?ref_=tt_trv_qu"
><span class="character">Jake Sully</span></a>:
[<span class="fine">Narrating</span>]
When I was lying in the V.A. hospital with a big hole blown through the middle of my life, I started having these dreams of flying. I was free. But sooner or later, you always have to wake up.
<br />        <a href="trivia?tab=qt&ref_=tt_trv_qu"
class="nobr" >See more</a> &raquo;
    </div>
                <hr />
     <div id="crazyCredits"  class="txt-block">
        <h4>Crazy Credits</h4>
There are no opening credits of any kind (outside of the 20th Century Fox title card). The title of the film doesn't appear on screen until the end of the movie.        <a href="trivia?tab=cz&ref_=tt_trv_cc"
class="nobr" >See more</a>  &raquo;
    </div>   
                <hr />
    <div id="connections" class="text-block">

        <a href="trivia?tab=mc&ref_=tt_trv_cnn"
class="nobr" >See more</a> &raquo;

    <div class="article" id="titleUserReviewsTeaser">
        <h2>User Reviews</h2>
        <div class="user-comments">
                <span itemprop="review" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">  
                    <strong itemprop="name">Technically outstanding. Originality: oh well....</strong>
                    <span itemprop="reviewRating" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Rating">
                        <meta itemprop="worstRating" content = "1" />
                        <meta itemprop="ratingValue" content="0" />
                        <meta itemprop="bestRating" content="10" />
                    </span>
                    <div class="comment-meta">
                        11 December 2009 | by <a href="/user/ur22516874/?ref_=tt_urv"
><span itemprop="author">elchocobollo</span></a>
                        <meta itemprop="datePublished" content="2009-12-11" />
                              (Spain)
                        &ndash; <a href="/user/ur22516874/comments?ref_=tt_urv"
>See all my reviews</a>
                    </div>
                    <div>
                        <p itemprop="reviewBody">Well, I just saw Avatar this morning, one of the press premieres which are running on these days. My opinion: you&#x27;ve seen this story a hundred times, but never like this. Finally 3D is what it&#x27;s supposed to be, an instrument at the service of the movie. You&#x27;ll enjoy the visual experience, no doubt.<br /><br />As for the story, some of the &#x22;inspirations&#x22; are so huge and so obvious that mentioning two or three of them would REALLY ruin the movie for you, and I&#x27;m not willing to do that. Lots of mysticism and ecology, if you like that stuff. If you&#x27;re 15 or so, you&#x27;ll have a great time thinking that it&#x27;s the first time somebody makes something like this. If you&#x27;re an experienced movie watcher, better leave your skepticism at the door, bring lots of pop corn and enjoy with the usual action-flick-with-moral-and-loads-of-clich&#xE9;s.<br /><br />I liked it, however: &#x22;the movie that re-invents movies&#x22;??? No way.</p>
                    </div>
                </span>
                <hr />
                <div class="yn" id="ynd_2172172">
                    2.137 of 3.314 people found this review helpful.&nbsp;

                    <button class="btn small" value="No" name="ynb_2172172_no" onclick="CS.TMD.user_review_vote(2172172, 'tt0499549', 'no');" >No</button>
